### Anti-patterns / Warnings

1. **"Don't build your prompts to accumulate context forever"**
   - The Mistake: Treating Claude.md as permanent archive; adding rules continuously; assuming all context additive to performance
   - Why It Fails: As models improve, accumulated context becomes noise; old rules designed for weaker models actively harm newer models; bloated context reduces signal
   - What to Do Instead: Iterate with minimal prompting; add rules only when model performance gaps emerge; delete rules liberally; treat context as ephemeral per-model state
   - Evidence: [DP5] Boris recommends deleting Claude.md and starting fresh with each model; add less with each iteration [cite:path=02_Extractions/2026-02/YCombinator_BorisChernyClaudeCode_2026-02-17.md;dp=5 -->

2. **"Don't over-invest in scaffolding features"**
   - The Mistake: Treating features designed to compensate for model limitations as long-term investments; expecting ROI over multi-year timeframes
   - Why It Fails: Scaffolding has 10-20% performance ceiling; becomes obsolete with next model; engineering effort compounded within quarters not years
   - What to Do Instead: Build scaffolding expecting obsolesce within 1-2 quarters; minimize scope; keep options open for removal; prioritize enduring features instead
   - Evidence: [DP4, DP8, DP14] plan mode, verbose logging, other scaffolding features approaching obsolesce [cite:path=02_Extractions/2026-02/YCombinator_BorisChernyClaudeCode_2026-02-17.md;dp=4 --> [cite:path=02_Extractions/2026-02/YCombinator_BorisChernyClaudeCode_2026-02-17.md;dp=8 --> [cite:path=02_Extractions/2026-02/YCombinator_BorisChernyClaudeCode_2026-02-17.md;dp=14 -->

### Numerical Rules-of-Thumb

1. **"The 150% Productivity Gain"**
   - The Rule: Anthropic engineering productivity per engineer grew 150% in 12 months since Claude Code launch
   - What It Means: Magnitude of improvement exceptional; baseline (Meta achieved 2% annual productivity improvement with hundreds of engineers); Anthropic achieved 150% in months with same team size doubled
   - When to Quote: When establishing productivity impact; justifying agentic tool investment; comparing to historical productivity gains
   - Precision Notes: Measured via PR volume normalized for team size; team doubled in size with 70% per-engineer growth
   - Conversation Hook: "Anthropic's per-engineer productivity went up 150% in one year. Meta considered 2% annual growth a major achievement."
   - Evidence: [DP11] organizational measurement from Anthropic, contextual comparison to historical standards [cite:path=02_Extractions/2026-02/YCombinator_BorisChernyClaudeCode_2026-02-17.md;dp=11 -->

2. **"The 4% Global Commit Share"**
   - The Rule: Claude Code represents 4% of all public code commits globally (as of Feb 2026)
   - What It Means: Magnitude of market penetration; dominance in code generation space; market concentration signal
   - When to Quote: When discussing market position; establishing competitive dominance; quantifying user adoption
   - Precision Notes: Public repository commits only; includes NASA Mars rover development; 70% of startups choose Claude as model of choice
   - Conversation Hook: "4% of all code written anywhere is written by Claude Code. That's market dominance."
   - Evidence: [DP13] Mercury data plus commit data; contextual evidence (NASA, startup surveys) [cite:path=02_Extractions/2026-02/YCombinator_BorisChernyClaudeCode_2026-02-17.md;dp=13 -->

3. **"The 70-90% Agent Code Range"**
   - The Rule: Broader Anthropic team achieves 70-90% Claude-written code; elite users (Boris) at 100%; team distribution reflects skill/adaptation variance
   - What It Means: Capability not limiting factor; adoption constrained by user willingness to adapt workflows, learn patterns, trust agent output; achieves ceiling at 100%
   - When to Quote: When discussing productivity range; explaining adoption variance; teaching that higher percentages achievable but require skill investment
   - Precision Notes: Anthropic team only; may not generalize; elite user (100%) represents maximum achievable currently
   - Conversation Hook: "Most Anthropic engineers land 70-90% agent-written code. The constraint isn't the model. It's the engineer's workflow adaptation."
   - Evidence: [DP11, DP12] direct organizational measurement; observed distribution [cite:path=02_Extractions/2026-02/YCombinator_BorisChernyClaudeCode_2026-02-17.md;dp=11 --> [cite:path=02_Extractions/2026-02/YCombinator_BorisChernyClaudeCode_2026-02-17.md;dp=12 -->

4. **"The 20 PRs Per Day Velocity"**
   - The Rule: Boris (100% Claude-written code) lands approximately 20 pull requests per day
   - What It Means: Velocity magnitude; enables high-volume iteration; suggests delivery cadence fundamentally shifts with agentic workflows
   - When to Quote: When illustrating productivity transformation; explaining velocity magnitude; contextualizing output acceleration
   - Precision Notes: Elite user outlier; 20 PRs/day reflects both code generation speed and different review culture; not typical across organizations
   - Conversation Hook: "Boris lands 20 PRs a day writing 100% Claude-generated code. That's velocity traditional engineering can't match."
   - Evidence: [DP11, DP12] direct statement of approximate PR volume [cite:path=02_Extractions/2026-02/YCombinator_BorisChernyClaudeCode_2026-02-17.md;dp=11 --> [cite:path=02_Extractions/2026-02/YCombinator_BorisChernyClaudeCode_2026-02-17.md;dp=12 -->

5. **"The 10-20% Scaffolding Ceiling"**
   - The Rule: Engineering effort to optimize around model limitations yields 10-20% performance improvement ceiling before next model renders optimization obsolete
   - What It Means: Asymmetric ROI on scaffolding; engineering effort best spent on enduring features not workarounds; highlights importance of capability improvement timing
   - When to Quote: When discussing engineering prioritization; explaining why scaffolding debt problematic; justifying feature design choices
   - Precision Notes: Proposed rule based on observed pattern; not empirically established constant; may vary across domains
   - Conversation Hook: "You can optimize around model limitations for maybe 10-20% gain. Then the model improves and your work is wasted."
   - Evidence: [DP4] core observation from capability improvement cycles [cite:path=02_Extractions/2026-02/YCombinator_BorisChernyClaudeCode_2026-02-17.md;dp=4 -->
